Nebraska\nhas placed\nemphasis\non successfully\nsecuring additional funds fi\'om non-EPSCoR\nand non-NASA\nsources.\nAERIAL researchers have aggressively\npursued additional funding opportunities\noffered by\nNASA, industry, and other agencies.\nThis report contains a summary of AERIAL\'s\nactivities\nand accomplishments\nduring its first three years of implementation.\nAERIAL\nis housed in the Division of Aeronautics\nand Transportation\nPolicy and\nResearch\nfacilities at the University of Nebraska at Omaha\'s (UNO) Aviation Institute.\nNASA\nNebraska EPSCoR\'s\nstructure has been well-suited\nto manage the interrelated nature of\nAERIAL\'s\n\ngoals and programmatic\n\nthe statewide\n\nemphasis\n\nobjectives,\n\nof its mission.\n\nthe varied interests\n\nAERIAL\n\npersonnel\n\nwork\n\nof AERIAL\n\nstakeholders,\n\nsynergistically\n\nand\n\nwith Nebraska\'s\n\nNSF EPSCoR\nprogram. AERIAL utilizes the existing NASA Nebraska\nEPSCoR management\nstructure - a structure that has a proven track record of success with NASA and a demonstrated\ncommitment\nto aeronautics and space science.\nThis structure efficiently\nand effectively\nmanages\nAERIAL\'s\ngoals and objectives,\nthe varied interests of AERIAL\nstakeholders,\nand the statewide\nemphases\nof its mission.\nThe administration\nof AERIAL continues to focus on the achievement\nof program goals\nand objectives,\nincluding ongoing identification\nof collaborative\nresearch opportunities\nwith\nNASA personnel, the support of AERIAL\'s\nresearch endeavors,\naerospace infrastructure, technology\ntransfer, the implementation\nincreased\n\ninclusion\n\nof Native\n\nAmericans\n\nin all program\n\nplanning process is ongoing as well, and is reviewed\nTechnical Advisory Committee\n(TAC).\nAs AERIAL\n\nstaff and researchers\n\ncomplete\n\nactivities.\n\nthe building\nof outreach\n\nThe AERIAL\n\nat the semi-annual\ntheir\n\nof Nebraska\'s\nactivities,\nand\n\nmeetings\n\nstrategic\nof the\n\nthird year of work, they look forward to\n\nachieving long-term systemic growth in Nebraska\'s aerospace research and industry.\nSuch\ndevelopment\nwill be evident long after NASA funding ceases.\nProgress toward this end has\nalready begun through the cultivation of innovative research and collaborations.\nContinued\nsuccess\nlevels\n\nof the AERIAL\nof refereed\n\ncollaborative\n\npublications,\n\nresearch\n\nteams (CRTs)\n\ninvited presentations,\n\nis anticipated\n\nand
